    20	export function build_attribute_effect(
    21	        attributes,
    22	        class_directives,
    23	        style_directives,
    24	        context,
    25	        element,
    26	        element_id
    27	) {
    28	        /** @type {ObjectExpression['properties']} */
    29	        const values = [];
    30	
    31	        const memoizer = new Memoizer();
    32	
    33	        for (const attribute of attributes) {
    34	                if (attribute.type === 'Attribute') {
    35	                        const { value } = build_attribute_value(attribute.value, context, (value, metadata) =>
    36	                                metadata.has_call || metadata.has_await ? memoizer.add(value, metadata.has_await) : value
    37	                        );
    38	
    39	                        if (
    40	                                is_event_attribute(attribute) &&
    41	                                (value.type === 'ArrowFunctionExpression' || value.type === 'FunctionExpression')
    42	                        ) {
    43	                                // Give the event handler a stable ID so it isn't removed and readded on every update
    44	                                const id = context.state.scope.generate('event_handler');
    45	                                context.state.init.push(b.var(id, value));
    46	                                values.push(b.init(attribute.name, b.id(id)));
    47	                        } else {
    48	                                values.push(b.init(attribute.name, value));
    49	                        }
    50	                } else {
    51	                        let value = /** @type {Expression} */ (context.visit(attribute));
    52	
    53	                        if (attribute.metadata.expression.has_call || attribute.metadata.expression.has_await) {
    54	                                value = memoizer.add(value, attribute.metadata.expression.has_await);
    55	                        }
    56	
    57	                        values.push(b.spread(value));
    58	                }
    59	        }
    60	
    61	        if (class_directives.length) {
    62	                values.push(
    63	                        b.prop(
    64	                                'init',
    65	                                b.array([b.id('$.CLASS')]),
    66	                                build_class_directives_object(class_directives, context, memoizer)
    67	                        )
    68	                );
    69	        }
    70	
    71	        if (style_directives.length) {
    72	                values.push(
    73	                        b.prop(

    76	                                build_style_directives_object(style_directives, context, memoizer)

    79	        }

    94	                                is_ignored(element, 'hydration_attribute_changed') && b.true

   100	/**
   101	 * @param {AST.Attribute['value']} value
   102	 * @param {ComponentContext} context
   103	 * @param {(value: Expression, metadata: ExpressionMetadata) => Expression} memoize
   104	 * @returns {{ value: Expression, has_state: boolean }}
   105	 */
   106	export function build_attribute_value(value, context, memoize = (value) => value) {
   107	        if (value === true) {
   108	                return { value: b.true, has_state: false };
   109	        }
   110	
   111	        if (!Array.isArray(value) || value.length === 1) {
   112	                const chunk = Array.isArray(value) ? value[0] : value;
   113	
   114	                if (chunk.type === 'Text') {
   115	                        return { value: b.literal(chunk.data), has_state: false };
   116	                }
   117	
   118	                let expression = build_expression(context, chunk.expression, chunk.metadata.expression);
   119	
   120	                return {
   121	                        value: memoize(expression, chunk.metadata.expression),

Let me check `is_prop_source` in utils.js again:

Looking at `/testbed/packages/svelte/src/compiler/phases/3-transform/client/utils.js`, lines 238-249:

```javascript
export function is_prop_source(binding, state) {
    return (
        (binding.kind === 'prop' || binding.kind === 'bindable_prop') &&
        (!state.analysis.runes ||
            state.analysis.accessors ||
            binding.reassigned ||
            binding.initial ||  // <-- This is key!
            // Until legacy mode is gone, we also need to use the prop source when only mutated is true,
            // because the parent could be a legacy component which needs coarse-grained reactivity
            binding.updated)
    );
}
```

So if a prop has `binding.initial` (which is the default value), then `is_prop_source` returns true, which means it will use `$.prop()` to create a prop source/getter.

3. Parent uses `<Child {onClick} />`

5. The `Identifier` visitor marks `has_state` based on whether the binding has state
6. The binding kind is 'prop', which is not 'static'
7. So `has_state` should be true

2025-12-26 22:44:15,901 - INFO - swea-agent-sveltejs__svelte-16504 - 💭 THOUGHT
Ah! This is important. Looking at lines 103-135:

When a prop binding has `is_prop_source` (which includes props with defaults), the transform is set to `{ read: b.call }`. This means that when you reference `onClick`, it will be transformed to `onClick()` - a function call.

However, when a prop binding doesn't have `is_prop_source`, it transforms to a direct member access like `$$props.onClick`.

So for a prop with a default:
- Parent creates: `const onClick = $.prop($$props, 'onClick', flags, () => {})`
- When referencing `onClick` in the parent, it transforms to `onClick()` (via the `b.call` transform)
- When passing to child: `<Child {onClick} />`, the transform should make it `onClick()`

But let me check the component.js code again for how identifiers are visited when they're attribute values:

 *
 * @param {ComponentContext} context
 * @param {Expression} expression
 * @param {ExpressionMetadata} metadata
 */
export function build_expression(context, expression, metadata, state = context.state) {
	const value = /** @type {Expression} */ (context.visit(expression, state));

	// Components not explicitly in legacy mode might be expected to be in runes mode (especially since we didn't
	// adjust this behavior until recently, which broke people's existing components), so we also bail in this case.
	// Kind of an in-between-mode.

		return value;

2025-12-26 22:45:40,765 - INFO - swea-agent-sveltejs__svelte-16504 - 💭 THOUGHT
Perfect! So when an identifier is visited in the transformation phase, it calls `build_getter` (line 39). Let me look at `build_getter` again more carefully:

From `/testbed/packages/svelte/src/compiler/phases/3-transform/client/utils.js` lines 31-46:

```javascript
export function build_getter(node, state) {
    if (Object.hasOwn(state.transform, node.name)) {
        const binding = state.scope.get(node.name);

        // don't transform the declaration itself
        if (node !== binding?.node) {
            return state.transform[node.name].read(node);
        }
    }

    return node;
}
```

So if there's a transform for the identifier, it calls `state.transform[node.name].read(node)`.

For props with defaults, the transform is `{ read: b.call }`, which means it returns a CallExpression like `onClick()`.

Now let's trace through what happens when this is passed to a child component:

1. Parent has `<Child {onClick} />`
2. The attribute value is just the identifier `onClick`
3. During attribute building, it visits the identifier
4. `build_getter` is called, which returns `onClick()` (a CallExpression)
5. This CallExpression is what gets passed to the child

So the child receives `onClick: onClick()` not `onClick: onClick`. This means the child gets the *result* of calling the prop getter, not the prop getter itself.

Here's the problem! When we call `onClick()` in the parent, we get the current value at that moment. But this is not reactive - the child won't know when the value changes because it's not subscribing to the prop, it's just getting a snapshot.

The fix should be to make sure that when passing props to children, we don't eagerly call the getter if it's a function prop. Instead, we should wrap it in a way that the child can reactively read it.

Let me examine this more carefully. The issue is specifically mentioned for function props with defaults. Let me think about what should happen:

1. Main component has `onClick={handler}` where handler is reactive
2. Parent gets it as prop with default: `let { onClick = () => {} } = $props()`
3. Parent passes to child: `<Child {onClick} />`

The parent's `onClick` is a getter that reads from `$$props.onClick` or returns the default. When the parent passes it to the child, the child should get either:
- A getter that will always return the current value
- Or the value should be wrapped in a way that makes it reactive

Let me check how this works when there's no default. Without a default, the transform would be (lines 124-134 in Program.js):

```javascript
context.state.transform[name] = {
    read: (_) => b.member(b.id('$$props'), key, key.type === 'Literal')
};
```

So without a default, `onClick` would be transformed to `$$props.onClick`, which is a direct member access that can be reactive.

With a default, `onClick` is transformed to `onClick()` (a call expression), which gets the current value but loses reactivity.

The solution is that when passing a prop with a default to a child component, we should not eagerly evaluate it. Instead, we should pass it in a way that maintains reactivity.

Looking at component.js lines 193-197:

```javascript
if (has_state) {
    push_prop(b.get(attribute.name, [b.return(value)]));
} else {
    push_prop(b.init(attribute.name, value));
}
```

When `has_state` is true, it wraps the value in a getter. This is correct. The problem is that `value` at this point is already `onClick()` (the result of calling the getter), not the getter itself.

The fix should be in how we determine the `value` for props. When the attribute value is an identifier that refers to a prop with a default, we should not call the getter, but instead wrap it properly.

Let me look at the specific code path. In component.js, the attribute value goes through `build_attribute_value`, which calls `build_expression`. `build_expression` visits the expression, which for an identifier calls `build_getter`, which applies the transform.

The issue is that the transform `{ read: b.call }` is too eager. It calls the prop immediately. But when passing to a child, we want to preserve the reactivity.

One solution is to detect when we're building an attribute value for a component and handle prop references specially. Let me think about where this check should go...

Actually, looking more carefully at the logic in component.js (lines 171-191):

```javascript
const { value, has_state } = build_attribute_value(
    attribute.value,
    context,
    (value, metadata) => {
        if (!metadata.has_state && !metadata.has_await) return value;
        
        // When we have a non-simple computation, anything other than an Identifier or Member expression,
        // then there's a good chance it needs to be memoized to avoid over-firing when read within the
        // child component (e.g. `active={i === index}`)
        const should_wrap_in_derived =
            metadata.has_await ||
            get_attribute_chunks(attribute.value).some((n) => {
                return (
                    n.type === 'ExpressionTag' &&
                    n.expression.type !== 'Identifier' &&
                    n.expression.type !== 'MemberExpression'
                );
            });
        
        return should_wrap_in_derived
            ? b.call('$.get', memoizer.add(value, metadata.has_await))
            : value;
    }
);
```

The memoize callback checks if the expression is an Identifier or MemberExpression and doesn't wrap it in derived if it is. But at this point, `value` is already `onClick()` (a CallExpression), not an Identifier.

The issue is that the transformation from `onClick` to `onClick()` happens during `context.visit(expression)` inside `build_expression`, before we get a chance to decide whether to wrap it or not.

I think the fix should be in the transform itself. When a prop has a default value, instead of transforming reads to `onClick()`, we should transform them differently when used in a component attribute context.

Actually, wait. Let me re-read the code. In `build_expression`:

```javascript
export function build_expression(context, expression, metadata, state = context.state) {
    const value = /** @type {Expression} */ (context.visit(expression, state));
    // ... rest of the function
}
```

It visits the expression, which applies the transform. For props with defaults, this turns `onClick` into `onClick()`.

But then in component.js, when checking whether to wrap in derived, it checks:

```javascript
n.expression.type !== 'Identifier' &&
n.expression.type !== 'MemberExpression'
```

This is checking the *original* expression type (from `attribute.value`), not the transformed one. So if the original expression was an Identifier, it won't wrap it in derived even though the transformed value is a CallExpression.

This is the bug! When the original expression is an Identifier that refers to a prop with a default, it becomes a CallExpression after transformation, but the code doesn't wrap it in derived because it checks the original expression type.

The fix should be to check the transformed value's type, not the original expression's type. Or, better yet, we should handle prop references specially.

Let me look at the actual code path more carefully. In build_attribute_value:

```javascript
let expression = build_expression(context, chunk.expression, chunk.metadata.expression);

return {
    value: memoize(expression, chunk.metadata.expression),
    has_state: chunk.metadata.expression.has_state || chunk.metadata.expression.has_await
};
```

So `expression` is the transformed value (e.g., `onClick()`), and then it calls `memoize(expression, chunk.metadata.expression)`.

In component.js, the memoize callback is:

```javascript
(value, metadata) => {
    if (!metadata.has_state && !metadata.has_await) return value;
    
    const should_wrap_in_derived =
        metadata.has_await ||
        get_attribute_chunks(attribute.value).some((n) => {
            return (
                n.type === 'ExpressionTag' &&
                n.expression.type !== 'Identifier' &&
                n.expression.type !== 'MemberExpression'
            );
        });
    
    return should_wrap_in_derived
        ? b.call('$.get', memoizer.add(value, metadata.has_await))
        : value;
}
```

So it checks `n.expression.type` which is the *original* expression type before transformation. If it's an Identifier, it doesn't wrap in derived.

But at this point, `value` is already `onClick()` (a CallExpression). So it returns `onClick()` without wrapping.

Then in component.js line 193:

```javascript
if (has_state) {
    push_prop(b.get(attribute.name, [b.return(value)]));
}
```

So it creates a getter that returns `onClick()`. This means every time the child reads the prop, it calls the parent's `onClick` getter, which should be reactive.

Wait, let me think about this again... If the child receives:

```javascript
{
    get onClick() { return onClick(); }
}
```

Then when the child reads `onClick`, it calls the getter, which calls the parent's `onClick()` function, which reads from `$$props.onClick` or returns the default.

Actually, this should work! Every time the child reads the prop, it calls the parent's getter. So if the parent's `$$props.onClick` changes, the child should see the new value.

Let me reconsider the problem. Maybe the issue is different. Let me re-read the PR description:

> If you have some component that takes a function as a prop and passes that on to child components, when the component provides a default value for that prop, changing the value of the prop will trigger reactivity with that component but will not trigger reactivity within any child components.

So the issue is that reactivity works in the parent but not in the child. The parent can react to changes in `onClick`, but when it passes `onClick` to the child, the child doesn't react to changes.

Let me think about what "react to changes" means. In Svelte 5 with runes, if you have:

```svelte
<script>
  let { onClick } = $props();
</script>
<button {onclick}>Click</button>
```

The `onclick` attribute should update when `onClick` changes. This happens because `onclick` is reactive - when you reference `onClick` in the template, it subscribes to changes.

But if the parent has:

```svelte
<script>
  let { onClick = () => {} } = $props();
</script>
<Child {onClick} />
```

And the parent's `onClick` changes, does the child's `onClick` update?

Let me trace through the compiled code:

Parent compiles to something like:

```javascript
const onClick = $.prop($$props, 'onClick', flags, () => {});
// When referencing onClick, it transforms to onClick()

// Child component call:
Child(anchor, {
    get onClick() { return onClick(); }
});
```

So the child receives a getter that calls the parent's `onClick()`. Every time the child reads its `onClick` prop, it calls the parent's getter. This should be reactive.

Wait, but there's a subtlety here. When does the child read its `onClick` prop? If the child has:

```svelte
<script>
  let { onClick } = $props();
</script>
<button {onclick}>Click</button>
```

The child compiles to:

```javascript
const onClick = $.prop($$props, 'onClick', flags);
// ...
<button onclick={onClick()}>
```

So the child reads `$$props.onClick` once when the component initializes, and then it reads `onClick()` every time the button is rendered.

Actually wait, I think I need to understand the problem better. Let me create a simple test case to understand what's happening. Let me actually compile some code to see what's generated.

2025-12-26 22:46:54,103 - INFO - swea-agent-sveltejs__svelte-16504 - 💭 THOUGHT
Perfect! Without a default value, the parent passes:

```javascript
{
    get onClick() {
        return $$props.onClick;
    }
}
```

This is a getter, so the child can reactively read the value. Every time the child accesses `$$props.onClick`, it calls the getter, which returns the current value from the parent's `$$props`.

But with a default value, the parent passes:

```javascript
{ onClick: onClick() }
```

This is not a getter - it's a static value (the result of calling `onClick()` at that moment). So the child gets a snapshot and can't react to changes.

Now I understand the bug! The issue is in how the parent compiles the attribute when the prop has a default value.

Looking back at the component.js code, when `has_state` is true, it should wrap in a getter:

```javascript
if (has_state) {
    push_prop(b.get(attribute.name, [b.return(value)]));
}
```

But for some reason, this isn't happening when the prop has a default. Let me check why `has_state` might be false in this case.

Let me modify my test to see if `has_state` is being set correctly:

import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';
import Child from './Child.svelte';

import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root = $.from_html(`<span> </span>`);

export default function Child($$anchor, $$props) {
	var span = root();
	var text = $.child(span, true);

	$.reset(span);
	$.template_effect(() => $.set_text(text, $$props.label));
	$.append($$anchor, span);
}

2025-12-26 22:47:57,062 - INFO - swea-agent-sveltejs__svelte-16504 - 💭 THOUGHT
Aha! With a string prop that has a default, the parent DOES pass a getter:

```javascript
{
    get label() {
        return label();
    }
}
```

So string props work correctly, but function props don't! Let me compare the two:

String prop:
- Parent: `let label = $.prop($$props, 'label', 3, 'default');`
- Parent passes: `get label() { return label(); }`

Function prop:
- Parent: `let onClick = $.prop($$props, 'onClick', 3, () => {...});`
- Parent passes: `onClick: onClick()`

The difference is that for the string prop, the parent wraps it in a getter, but for the function prop, it doesn't.

This suggests that `has_state` is being calculated differently for function props vs string props. Let me check the Identifier visitor again:

From `/testbed/packages/svelte/src/compiler/phases/2-analyze/visitors/Identifier.js` lines 94-97:

```javascript
context.state.expression.has_state ||=
    binding.kind !== 'static' &&
    !binding.is_function() &&  // <-- This is the problem!
    !context.state.scope.evaluate(node).is_known;
```

The `has_state` is set to false if `binding.is_function()` is true! This is the bug. When a prop is a function, even though it's a prop and should be reactive, `has_state` is set to false because the binding is considered a function.

Let me check what `binding.is_function()` does. Looking at the binding type, it should check if the binding's initial value is a function. For a prop like `let { onClick = () => {} } = $props()`, the binding's initial value is `() => {}`, which is a function, so `is_function()` returns true.

This means that function props with defaults are not marked as having state, even though they are reactive props!

The fix should be to not exclude function props from having state. Props should always be considered as having state (unless they can be statically evaluated), regardless of whether the default value is a function.

	}

	/**
	 * @returns {this is Binding & { initial: ArrowFunctionExpression | FunctionDeclaration | FunctionExpression }}
	 */
	is_function() {
		if (this.updated) {
			// even if it's reassigned to another function,
			// we can't use it directly as e.g. an event handler
			return false;
		}

		const type = this.initial?.type;

		return (
			type === 'ArrowFunctionExpression' ||
			type === 'FunctionExpression' ||
			type === 'FunctionDeclaration'
		);
	}
}

Testing function prop with default value passed to child component

=== MAIN ===
import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';
import Parent from './Parent.svelte';

var root = $.from_html(`<p> </p> <!>`, 1);

export default function Main($$anchor) {
	let count = $.state(0);

	function handler() {
		$.update(count);
	}

	var fragment = root();
	var p = $.first_child(fragment);
	var text = $.child(p);

	$.reset(p);

	var node = $.sibling(p, 2);

	Parent(node, { onClick: handler });
	$.template_effect(() => $.set_text(text, `Count: ${$.get(count) ?? ''}`));
	$.append($$anchor, fragment);
}

=== PARENT ===
import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';
import Child from './Child.svelte';

export default function Parent($$anchor, $$props) {
	let onClick = $.prop($$props, 'onClick', 3, () => {});

	Child($$anchor, {
		get onClick() {
			return onClick();
		}
	});
}

=== CHILD ===
import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root = $.from_html(`<button>Click</button>`);

export default function Child($$anchor, $$props) {
	var button = root();

	button.__click = function (...$$args) {
		$$props.onClick?.apply(this, $$args);
	};

	$.append($$anchor, button);
}

$.delegate(['click']);

import { test } from '../../test';

export default test({
	get props() {
		return {
			foo: 'x',
			bar: 'z',
			default1: 1,
			default2: undefined
		};
	},

		assert.htmlEqual(target.innerHTML, `y 1 2 3 w`);
	}
});

+        let i = context.path.length;
+        let parent = /** @type {Expression} */ (context.path[--i]);
+
+        if (!is_reference(node, parent)) {
+                return;
+        }
+
+        mark_subtree_dynamic(context.path);
+
+        // If we are using arguments outside of a function, then throw an error
+        if (
+                node.name === 'arguments' &&
+                !context.path.some((n) => n.type === 'FunctionDeclaration' || n.type === 'FunctionExpression')
+        ) {
+                e.invalid_arguments_usage(node);
+        }
+
+        // `$$slots` exists even in runes mode
+        if (node.name === '$$slots') {
+                context.state.analysis.uses_slots = true;
+        }
+
+        if (context.state.analysis.runes) {
+                if (
+                        is_rune(node.name) &&
+                        context.state.scope.get(node.name) === null &&
+                        context.state.scope.get(node.name.slice(1))?.kind !== 'store_sub'
+                ) {
+                        /** @type {Expression} */
+                        let current = node;
+                        let name = node.name;
+
+                        while (parent.type === 'MemberExpression') {
+                                if (parent.computed) e.rune_invalid_computed_property(parent);
+                                name += `.${/** @type {Identifier} */ (parent.property).name}`;
+
+                                current = parent;
+                                parent = /** @type {Expression} */ (context.path[--i]);
+
+                                if (!is_rune(name)) {
+                                        if (name === '$effect.active') {
+                                                e.rune_renamed(parent, '$effect.active', '$effect.tracking');
+                                        }
+
+                                        if (name === '$state.frozen') {
+                                                e.rune_renamed(parent, '$state.frozen', '$state.raw');
+                                        }
+
+                                        if (name === '$state.is') {
+                                                e.rune_removed(parent, '$state.is');
+                                        }
+
+                                        e.rune_invalid_name(parent, name);
+                                }
+                        }
+
+                        if (parent.type !== 'CallExpression') {
+                                e.rune_missing_parentheses(current);
+                        }
+                }
+        }
+
+        let binding = context.state.scope.get(node.name);
+
+        if (!context.state.analysis.runes) {
+                if (node.name === '$$props') {
+                        context.state.analysis.uses_props = true;
+                }
+
+                if (node.name === '$$restProps') {
+                        context.state.analysis.uses_rest_props = true;
+                }
+        }
+
+        if (binding) {
+                if (context.state.expression) {
+                        context.state.expression.dependencies.add(binding);
+                        context.state.expression.references.add(binding);
+                        context.state.expression.has_state ||=
+                                binding.kind !== 'static' &&
+                                // Props should be considered as having state even if they're functions,
+                                // because they're reactive and can change when passed to child components
+                                (binding.kind === 'prop' || binding.kind === 'bindable_prop' || !binding.is_function()) &&
+                                !context.state.scope.evaluate(node).is_known;
+                }
+
+                if (
+                        context.state.analysis.runes &&
+                        node !== binding.node &&
+                        context.state.function_depth === binding.scope.function_depth &&
+                        // If we have $state that can be proxied or frozen and isn't re-assigned, then that means
+                        // it's likely not using a primitive value and thus this warning isn't that helpful.
+                        ((binding.kind === 'state' &&
+                                (binding.reassigned ||
+                                        (binding.initial?.type === 'CallExpression' &&
+                                                binding.initial.arguments.length === 1 &&
+                                                binding.initial.arguments[0].type !== 'SpreadElement' &&
+                                                !should_proxy(binding.initial.arguments[0], context.state.scope)))) ||
+                                binding.kind === 'raw_state' ||
+                                binding.kind === 'derived') &&
+                        // We're only concerned with reads here
+                        (parent.type !== 'AssignmentExpression' || parent.left !== node) &&
+                        parent.type !== 'UpdateExpression'
+                ) {
+                        let type = 'closure';
+
+                        let i = context.path.length;
+                        while (i--) {
+                                const parent = context.path[i];
+
+                                if (
+                                        parent.type === 'ArrowFunctionExpression' ||
+                                        parent.type === 'FunctionDeclaration' ||
+                                        parent.type === 'FunctionExpression'
+                                ) {
+                                        break;
+                                }
+
+                                if (
+                                        parent.type === 'CallExpression' &&
+                                        parent.arguments.includes(/** @type {any} */ (context.path[i + 1]))
+                                ) {
+                                        const rune = get_rune(parent, context.state.scope);
+
+                                        if (rune === '$state' || rune === '$state.raw') {
+                                                type = 'derived';
+                                                break;
+                                        }
+                                }
+                        }
+
+                        w.state_referenced_locally(node, node.name, type);
+                }
+
+                if (
+                        context.state.reactive_statement &&
+                        binding.scope === context.state.analysis.module.scope &&
+                        binding.reassigned
+                ) {
+                        w.reactive_declaration_module_script_dependency(node);
+                }
+        }
 }

diff --git a/packages/svelte/tests/runtime-runes/samples/props-function-default-child-reactivity/_config.js b/packages/svelte/tests/runtime-runes/samples/props-function-default-child-reactivity/_config.js

+import { flushSync } from 'svelte';
+import { test } from '../../test';
+
+export default test({
+html: `
+<p>Count: 0</p>
+<p>Count2: 100</p>
+<button>Click</button>
+<button>Reset count to 50</button>
+<button>Reset count2 to 150</button>
+`,
+
+async test({ assert, target }) {
+const [clickBtn, resetBtn, reset2Btn] = target.querySelectorAll('button');
+
+// Click the button - should trigger handler and increment count
+flushSync(() => {
+clickBtn?.click();
+});
+
+assert.htmlEqual(
+target.innerHTML,
+`
+<p>Count: 1</p>
+<p>Count2: 100</p>
+<button>Click</button>
+<button>Reset count to 50</button>
+<button>Reset count2 to 150</button>
+`
+);
+
+// Reset count to 50
+flushSync(() => {
+resetBtn?.click();
+});
+
+assert.htmlEqual(
+target.innerHTML,
+`
+<p>Count: 50</p>
+<p>Count2: 100</p>
+<button>Click</button>
+<button>Reset count to 50</button>
+<button>Reset count2 to 150</button>
+`
+);
+
+// Click again - should increment from 50 to 51
+flushSync(() => {
+clickBtn?.click();
+});
+
+assert.htmlEqual(
+target.innerHTML,
+`
+<p>Count: 51</p>
+<p>Count2: 100</p>
+<button>Click</button>
+<button>Reset count to 50</button>
+<button>Reset count2 to 150</button>
+`
+);
+}
+});

+import { compile } from '/testbed/packages/svelte/src/compiler/index.js';
+
+const parentSource = `
+<script>
+  import Child from './Child.svelte';
+  let { onClick = () => {} } = $props();
+</script>
+<Child {onClick} />
+`;
+
+const childSource = `
+<script>
+  let { onClick } = $props();
+</script>
+<button onclick={onClick}>Click</button>
+`;
+
+console.log('=== PARENT ===');
+try {
+  const parentResult = compile(parentSource, { filename: 'Parent.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  console.log(parentResult.js.code);
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('Parent compile error:', error.message);
+}
+
+console.log('\n=== CHILD ===');
+try {
+  const childResult = compile(childSource, { filename: 'Child.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  console.log(childResult.js.code);
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('Child compile error:', error.message);
+}

+import { compile } from '/testbed/packages/svelte/src/compiler/index.js';

+console.log('Testing function prop with default value passed to child component\n');
+
+const mainSource = `
+<script>
+  import Parent from './Parent.svelte';
+  
+  let count = $state(0);
+  
+  function handler() {
+    count++;
+  }
+</script>
+
+<p>Count: {count}</p>
+<Parent onClick={handler} />
+`;
+
+const parentSource = `
+<script>
+  import Child from './Child.svelte';
+  let { onClick = () => {} } = $props();
+</script>
+
+<Child {onClick} />
+`;
+
+const childSource = `
+<script>
+  let { onClick } = $props();
+</script>
+<button onclick={onClick}>Click</button>
+`;
+
+console.log('=== MAIN ===');
+try {
+  const mainResult = compile(mainSource, { filename: 'Main.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  console.log(mainResult.js.code);
+  console.log();
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('Main compile error:', error.message);
+}
+
+console.log('=== PARENT ===');
+try {
+  const parentResult = compile(parentSource, { filename: 'Parent.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  console.log(parentResult.js.code);
+  console.log();
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('Parent compile error:', error.message);
+}
+
+console.log('=== CHILD ===');
+try {
+  const childResult = compile(childSource, { filename: 'Child.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  console.log(childResult.js.code);
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('Child compile error:', error.message);

diff --git a/test_fix.js b/test_fix.js

@@ -0,0 +1,108 @@
+import { compile, VERSION } from '/testbed/packages/svelte/src/compiler/index.js';
+
+console.log('Svelte version:', VERSION);
+console.log('\nTest: Function props with defaults should maintain reactivity in child components\n');
+
+// Test 1: Function prop with default
+console.log('=== Test 1: Function prop with default ===');
+const test1Parent = `
+<script>
+  import Child from './Child.svelte';
+  let { onClick = () => {} } = $props();
+</script>
+<Child {onClick} />
+`;
+
+try {
+  const result = compile(test1Parent, { filename: 'Parent.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  const code = result.js.code;
+  
+  // Check if the parent passes onClick as a getter
+  if (code.includes('get onClick()')) {
+    console.log('✓ PASS: Parent passes onClick as a getter');
+    console.log('  Code snippet:', code.match(/get onClick\(\).*?\}/s)?.[0]);
+  } else {
+    console.log('✗ FAIL: Parent does not pass onClick as a getter');
+    console.log('  Full code:', code);
+  }
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('✗ FAIL: Compilation error:', error.message);
+}
+
+// Test 2: Function prop without default (should also use getter)
+console.log('\n=== Test 2: Function prop without default ===');
+const test2Parent = `
+<script>
+  import Child from './Child.svelte';
+  let { onClick } = $props();
+</script>
+<Child {onClick} />
+`;
+
+try {
+  const result = compile(test2Parent, { filename: 'Parent.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  const code = result.js.code;
+  
+  if (code.includes('get onClick()')) {
+    console.log('✓ PASS: Parent passes onClick as a getter');
+  } else {
+    console.log('✗ FAIL: Parent does not pass onClick as a getter');
+    console.log('  Full code:', code);
+  }
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('✗ FAIL: Compilation error:', error.message);
+}
+
+// Test 3: String prop with default (should use getter)
+console.log('\n=== Test 3: String prop with default ===');
+const test3Parent = `
+<script>
+  import Child from './Child.svelte';
+  let { label = 'default' } = $props();
+</script>
+<Child {label} />
+`;
+
+try {
+  const result = compile(test3Parent, { filename: 'Parent.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  const code = result.js.code;
+  
+  if (code.includes('get label()')) {
+    console.log('✓ PASS: Parent passes label as a getter');
+  } else {
+    console.log('✗ FAIL: Parent does not pass label as a getter');
+    console.log('  Full code:', code);
+  }
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('✗ FAIL: Compilation error:', error.message);
+}
+
+// Test 4: Non-prop function (should not use getter for the function itself)
+console.log('\n=== Test 4: Non-prop function ===');
+const test4Parent = `
+<script>
+  import Child from './Child.svelte';
+  function myFunc() {}
+</script>
+<Child onClick={myFunc} />
+`;
+
+try {
+  const result = compile(test4Parent, { filename: 'Parent.svelte', generate: 'client' });
+  const code = result.js.code;
+  
+  // For non-prop functions, the reference doesn't need a getter since it's not reactive
+  // But we should still pass it properly to the child
+  if (code.includes('onClick: myFunc') || code.includes('get onClick()')) {
+    console.log('✓ PASS: Parent passes myFunc to child');
+    console.log('  Code snippet:', code.match(/onClick:.*?[,}]/s)?.[0]);
+  } else {
+    console.log('? INFO: Check how non-prop functions are passed');
+    console.log('  Full code:', code);
+  }
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('✗ FAIL: Compilation error:', error.message);
+}
+
+console.log('\n=== Summary ===');
+console.log('All tests completed. Check results above.');
